## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of concentration dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t, which is the fundamental problem in chemical kinetics rate law identification. The explicit time dependence may indicate reversible reactions, complex mechanisms, or time-varying conditions.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 (constant consumption/production rate)
- First-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A (unimolecular decay or first-order kinetics)
- Second-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular same-species reaction)
- nth-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate law)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse first-order reaction with equilibrium)
- Mixed order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (competing first and second order pathways)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme or saturation kinetics)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalysis, A catalyzes its own formation from substrate)
- Fractional order: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (fractional order with offset)
- Time-dependent rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying rate constant, e.g., temperature ramp)
- Reversible with explicit solution form: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (rate depending on another species expressed via t)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (substrate inhibition)
- Cooperative kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (Hill-type cooperative binding)
- Combined time-concentration: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * t**c2 (power-law in both time and concentration)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Pure concentration dependence (no explicit t) suggests a closed autonomous system with a simple rate law dA/dt = f(A)
- If dA/dt depends on both A and t explicitly, another reacting species (e.g., B) has been eliminated using its analytical time-dependence, embedding t into the rate expression
- Rational forms in A (e.g., A/(K+A)) indicate enzyme-like or surface-catalyzed reactions with saturation at high concentrations
- Quadratic terms A*(c-A) indicate autocatalytic or logistic growth where the reaction is self-accelerating then self-limiting
- Negative coefficients on concentration power terms indicate consumption (reactant depletion), while positive coefficients indicate production or autocatalysis
- Half-integer or fractional powers of A (e.g., A**0.5) arise in chain reaction mechanisms involving radical intermediates
- Exponential dependence on t may indicate coupling to a species that itself follows first-order kinetics (pseudo-first-order elimination)
- A rate law with A**2 in the denominator suggests strong product or substrate inhibition mechanisms

GT Equivalence Verification (CRK15)

GT: -c0*sqrt(A) - c1*A*exp(-c2*_s*t) + c3*_t*sin(log(A + c4))
Candidate formulas: 50

I need to determine if any candidate formula can match the GT:

**GT:** `-0.12072*sqrt(A) - 0.12072*A*exp(-0.06862*t) + 0.85374*sin(log(A + 1))`

The GT has three distinct functional components:
1. `-0.12072*sqrt(A)` — a square root term
2. `-0.12072*A*exp(-0.06862*t)` — an exponential decay times A
3. `0.85374*sin(log(A + 1))` — sine of logarithm

The key challenge is the `sin(log(A+1))` term. This is a very specific function that cannot be represented by combinations of `log`, `exp`, polynomials, or rational functions of A.

Let me scan the candidates for any that contain a `sin` term:

- **Candidate 19**: `A*c0*exp(c1*t) + c2*sin(A*c3 + c4) + c5*log(A*c6 + 1) + c7*exp(A*c8) + c9`
  - This has `sin(A*c3 + c4)`, which is `sin` of a linear function of A, not `sin(log(A+1))`. These are fundamentally different functions and cannot match.

- **Candidate 49**: `A*c0/(c1 + t)**2 + c2*sin(A*c3 + c4) + c5*exp(c6*t) + c7/(A + c8)**2 + c9`
  - Same issue: `sin(A*c3 + c4)` ≠ `sin(log(A+1))`.

No candidate contains `sin(log(...))`.

Now, could `sin(log(A+1))` be approximated or exactly represented by other terms? For exact equivalence over all A, `sin(log(A+1))` is a transcendental oscillating function that cannot be written as any finite combination of:
- Powers of A (`A^c`, `sqrt(A)`)
- Logarithms (`log(A*c + 1)`)
- Exponentials of A (`exp(A*c)`)
- Rational functions of A
- Products of the above

The function `sin(log(A+1))` oscillates (albeit slowly for large A), while `log`, `exp`, power functions, and rational functions are all monotonic for large enough A. No finite sum of such monotonic functions can reproduce the oscillatory behavior of `sin(log(A+1))`.

**Candidate 2** has `sqrt(A)*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + A*c3 + c4*log(A*c5 + 1) + c6*log(A*c7 + 1) + c8`. This has the sqrt(A) and A*exp terms, but uses log terms instead of sin(log(...)), which cannot match.

**Candidate 7** has `A**c3*c4 + A**c5*c6` power terms plus log, but still no sin(log).

**Candidate 30/31** have `A**c3*c4` which could give sqrt(A) with c3=0.5, plus log terms, but still missing sin(log).

None of the candidates contain `sin(log(...))` or any mechanism to produce the oscillatory behavior of `sin(log(A+1))`.

[NO MATCH]

Conclusion: No match

GT: -c0*sqrt(A) - c1*A*exp(-c2*_s*t) + c3*_t*sin(log(A + c4))
Candidates evaluated: 50

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.12072*sqrt(A) - 0.12072*A*exp(-0.06862*t) + 0.85374*sin(log(A + 1))`

The GT has three basis functions:
1. `sqrt(A)` = `A^0.5`
2. `A*exp(c*t)` (with negative coefficient in exponent)
3. `sin(log(A + 1))`

Key observation: The GT contains `sin(log(A+1))`, which is a very specific nonlinear function. None of the candidates can produce `sin(log(...))` unless they explicitly contain `sin` composed with `log`.

Let me scan all candidates for the presence of `sin(log(...))` or equivalent:

Looking through all 50 candidates:
- Most candidates use combinations of: `A*exp(c*t)`, `A*c`, `A^c`, `log(A*c+1)`, `exp(A*c)`, `t/(A+c)^n`, `1/(A+c)^n`, `sin(A*c+c)`, `t^c`, `log(c*t+1)`, `A/(c+t)^2`
- **Candidate 19** has `sin(A*c3 + c4)` — this is `sin(linear in A)`, NOT `sin(log(A+1))`
- **Candidate 49** has `sin(A*c3 + c4)` — same issue

None of the candidates contain `sin(log(...))`. The function `sin(log(A+1))` cannot be expressed as any combination of:
- polynomials in A
- `log(A+1)` (without sin)
- `exp(A*c)`
- `sin(A*c + c)` (sin of linear, not sin of log)
- `A^c` (power functions)
- rational functions of A and t

By the principle of linear independence of basis functions, `sin(log(A+1))` is linearly independent from all these other function types. Since the coefficient of `sin(log(A+1))` in the GT is 0.85374 (non-zero), no candidate can match.

Let me verify: Could `sin(log(A+1))` be approximated by `log(A+1)` terms? No — we need EXACT equivalence, not approximation. `sin(x) ≠ c*x` for all x.

Could multiple `log(A*c+1)` terms combine to form `sin(log(A+1))`? No — sums of logarithms are logarithms of products, never producing a sine function.

Could `exp(A*c)` terms produce `sin(log(A+1))`? No — exponentials of A cannot produce sine of log of A.

Could `A^c` with complex c produce sin? In principle `A^{ic}` involves sin/cos of log(A), but the candidates specify real constants, and `A^c` with real c gives real power functions, not oscillatory functions.

Let me double-check Candidate 19 more carefully:
`A*c0*exp(c1*t) + c2*sin(A*c3 + c4) + c5*log(A*c6 + 1) + c7*exp(A*c8) + c9`

This has `sin(A*c3 + c4)` which is `sin(linear in A)`. The GT needs `sin(log(A+1))`. These are fundamentally different functions — `sin(c3*A + c4)` oscillates with period `2π/c3` in A, while `sin(log(A+1))` has logarithmically-spaced oscillations. They cannot be equal for all A.

Therefore, **no candidate matches**.
